<p><b>Miralem Pjani</b> (<small>Bosnian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[mirâlem pjânit]</a></span>; born 2 April 1990) is a Bosnian professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> for Spanish club <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina national team</a>.
</p><p>Pjani started his professional career at <a href="/wiki/FC_Metz" title="FC Metz">Metz</a> being there for one season. He signed for side <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a> in 2008 before signing for <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> in 2011 after three seasons at Lyon. During his time in Rome, Pjani came to be recognized as one of the best midfielders in Serie A. In 2016, Pjani joined <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a>, and has since been considered an integral player for the team, winning four Serie A titles, two <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italias</a>, and being named in the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year" title="Serie A Team of the Year">Serie A Team of the Year</a> for <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year#2015–16" title="Serie A Team of the Year">2015–16</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year#2016–17" title="Serie A Team of the Year">2016–17</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year#2017–18" title="Serie A Team of the Year">2017–18</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year#2018–19" title="Serie A Team of the Year">2018–19</a> seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He was also named in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League#Squad_of_the_Season" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">2016–17 UEFA Champions League Squad of the Season</a>, for his role in Juventus's run to the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2017 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Pjani joined Barcelona in September 2020.
</p><p>A former Luxembourgish youth international, Pjani made his senior international debut for Bosnia and Herzegovina in 2008, earning over 90 <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">caps</a> and scoring 15 goals since. He represented the nation at their first major tournament, the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p><p>In 2015, he was ranked 55th in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a>'</i>s list of "The 100 best footballers in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
In 2019, he was ranked 50th in the same list.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Pjani was born on 2 April 1990 in <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">Tuzla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Socialist Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, in what was then <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>); to father Fahrudin and mother Fatima. He developed an interest in footballing through his father, a former third division footballer in Yugoslavia,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and began his football career in Luxembourg following his family's arrival to the country shortly before the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> While in Luxembourg, Pjani often attended training sessions and matches with his father.<sup id="cite_ref-pjanic_guardian_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pjanic_guardian-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> At the age of seven, his father discovered that he had talent and an interest in football and allowed his son to join local club FC Schifflange 95 in <a href="/wiki/Schifflange" title="Schifflange">Schifflange</a>. While at Schifflange, Pjani drew interest from several Belgian, Dutch and German clubs, but agreed to join <a href="/wiki/FC_Metz" title="FC Metz">Metz</a> in France in 2004. Pjani was recommended by former Metz player and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg international</a> <a href="/wiki/Guy_Hellers" title="Guy Hellers">Guy Hellers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metz">Metz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Metz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Pjani joined Metz at age 14 on a youth contract and spent approximately three years in the club's academy. In the 2005–06 season, he played on the under-16 team that won the <i>Championnat National des 16 ans</i> and, following the season, signed a five-year <i>élite</i> contract with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After spending the 2006–07 season with the club's under-18 team, Pjani was promoted to the club's amateur team in the <a href="/wiki/Championnat_National_2" title="Championnat National 2">Championnat de France Amateur</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Ligue_1" title="2007–08 Ligue 1">2007–08 season</a>. He appeared in the first two matches of the campaign before earning a call up to the senior team by manager Francis De Taddeo. Pjani made his professional football debut, at the age of 17, on 18 August 2007 in a league match against <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a>. He appeared as a substitute in a 0–0 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The following week, he earned his first start in a 2–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Stade_Rennais_F.C." title="Stade Rennais F.C.">Rennes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a string of respectable appearances, on 30 November 2007, Pjani signed his first professional contract agreeing to a three-year deal, tying him to Metz until 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> After becoming professional, he was assigned the <a href="/wiki/Squad_number_(association_football)" title="Squad number (association football)">number 15 shirt</a>. Pjani scored his first professional goal for Metz on 15 December 2007 in a 2–1 defeat against <a href="/wiki/FC_Sochaux-Montb%C3%A9liard" title="FC Sochaux-Montbéliard">Sochaux</a> converting on a penalty in the 88th minute, thus becoming one of the youngest players to score a goal in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> history.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Among his other positive performances included converting another penalty in a 2–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">Nice</a> and scoring on the final day of the season against <a href="/wiki/Le_Mans_FC" title="Le Mans FC">Le Mans</a> in a thrilling 4–3 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani's play in the <a href="/wiki/Coupe_de_France" title="Coupe de France">Coupe de France</a> was with distinction as well appearing in and starting all four matches the club contested. He assisted on several goals in the club's 6–1 demolition of <a href="/wiki/Vesoul_Haute-Sa%C3%B4ne" class="mw-redirect" title="Vesoul Haute-Saône">Vesoul Haute-Saône</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In the ensuing round, Pjani scored the final goal in Metz's 3–0 triumph over <a href="/wiki/RC_Strasbourg" class="mw-redirect" title="RC Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> and played the full 90 minutes in the club's 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Lorient" title="FC Lorient">Lorient</a> in the Round of 16 helping the club who were, at the time, struggling in domestic play, reach the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Coupe_de_France#Quarterfinals" title="2007–08 Coupe de France">quarterfinals of the Coupe de France</a>. Metz were eventually eliminated by the eventual champions Lyon.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
In total, Pjani made 38 appearances and scored 5 goals with Metz. For his efforts, he was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Ligue_1#Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="2007–08 Ligue 1">Ligue 1 Young Player of the Year award</a>, won by <a href="/wiki/Hatem_Ben_Arfa" title="Hatem Ben Arfa">Hatem Ben Arfa</a>.
</p><p>Though Pjani was in great form throughout the season, Metz still suffered relegation back to <a href="/wiki/Ligue_2" title="Ligue 2">Ligue 2</a>, prompting speculation that the young star would move to any of a host of clubs, with English clubs <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, Spanish clubs <a href="/wiki/F.C._Barcelona" class="mw-redirect" title="F.C. Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, Italian clubs <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internazionale" class="mw-redirect" title="Internazionale">Inter</a>, and French club <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a> vying for his services.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyon">Lyon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lyon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Metz received numerous offers for the player's services, on 6 June 2008, Pjani and Metz both reached an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Olympique Lyonnais</a> for the transfer of the player.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Pjani agreed to a five-year contract, while the transfer fee was priced at €7.5 million plus future incentives.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Labeled as the future replacement for the ageing <a href="/wiki/Juninho_Pernambucano" title="Juninho Pernambucano">Juninho</a>, Pjani was initially given the number 12 shirt, but switched to the number 18 for <a href="/wiki/Pre-season" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-season">pre-season</a> and made his club debut in the team's <a href="/wiki/2008_Troph%C3%A9e_des_Champions" title="2008 Trophée des Champions">Trophée des Champions</a> defeat to <a href="/wiki/FC_Girondins_de_Bordeaux" title="FC Girondins de Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He made his league debut in the opening league match of the season against <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_FC" title="Toulouse FC">Toulouse</a> playing the entire match in a 3–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Pjani's debut season with Lyon was cut in half after fracturing his <a href="/wiki/Fibula" title="Fibula">fibula</a> in a match against Sochaux in October 2008, as a result of a bad tackle by <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Dalmat" title="Stéphane Dalmat">Stéphane Dalmat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Despite initially being diagnosed as missing a month, he missed two months and made his return on 3 January 2009 in the club's 6–0 thrashing of amateur club <a href="/wiki/US_Concarneau" title="US Concarneau">US Concarneau</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Coupe_de_France#Round_of_64" title="2008–09 Coupe de France">Coupe de France</a> playing 66 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Olympique_Lyonnais_season" title="2009–10 Olympique Lyonnais season">2009–10 season</a>, Pjani switched to the number 8 shirt, formerly worn by his predecessor and Lyon great Juninho. He started the season strong scoring his first career goal for Lyon on a <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> in Lyon's playoff round match against Belgian club <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2009–10 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. Lyon won the match 5–1.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A couple of days later, he scored his first career league goal for the club, in which his side won 3–0 at <a href="/wiki/AJ_Auxerre" title="AJ Auxerre">Auxerre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Pjani continued his stellar play in the Champions League scoring the only goal in the club's opening group stage match against Italian club <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In the club's second group stage match against Hungarian club <a href="/wiki/Debreceni_VSC" title="Debreceni VSC">Debreceni</a>, he scored again, via free kick, and also assisted on two other goals in the club's 4–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 10 March 2010, Pjani scored the equalizing goal in Lyon's 1–1 draw with Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in the second leg of their first knockout round tie in the UEFA Champions League. The draw sent Lyon through to the quarter-finals due to their 1–0 win in the first leg at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_Gerland" title="Stade de Gerland">Stade Gerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani began the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Olympique_Lyonnais_season" title="2010–11 Olympique Lyonnais season">2010–11 season</a> as a starter and featured in the team's first three games. However, following the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Yoann_Gourcuff" title="Yoann Gourcuff">Yoann Gourcuff</a>, he began appearing as a substitute and, subsequently, appeared as a substitute in the team's next seven league matches. On 29 September 2010, Pjani scored his first goal of the season in the team's 3–1 win over Israeli club <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Hapoel Tel Aviv F.C.">Hapoel Tel Aviv</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> As a result of his good form, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Puel" title="Claude Puel">Claude Puel</a> began experimenting playing both Gourcuff and Pjani in the midfield, but after playing the two in a 2–0 win over Portuguese club <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a> in the Champions League and a 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/Stade_Rennais_F.C." title="Stade Rennais F.C.">Rennes</a> in the league, this tactic was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roma">Roma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Roma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="915" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pjani playing for <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> in 2012</div></div></div>
<p>On 31 August 2011, Pjani agreed a four-year deal with Italian club <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>, for an €11 million transfer fee.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Roma against <a href="/wiki/U.S._Lecce" title="U.S. Lecce">Lecce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani started the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_A.S._Roma_season" title="2012–13 A.S. Roma season">2012–13 season</a> mostly on the bench. He got his chance in a <i><a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Capitale" title="Derby della Capitale">Derby della Capitale</a></i> and scored a goal.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> From that game, he started playing regularly and scored one more goal in 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Torino_F.C." title="Torino F.C.">Torino</a> and one in the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> against <a href="/wiki/Atalanta_B.C." title="Atalanta B.C.">Atalanta</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_A.S._Roma_season" title="2013–14 A.S. Roma season">2013–14 season</a>, under new Roma coach <a href="/wiki/Rudi_Garcia" title="Rudi Garcia">Rudi Garcia</a>, he was a starter in the 4–3–3 midfield, playing a key role to the team's Serie A record of ten wins in the first ten season matches.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani scored 6 goals and provided 6 assists in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Serie_A" title="2013–14 Serie A">2013–14 Serie A season</a>. On 25 April 2014, he scored the first goal in Roma's 2–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>; the goal was a wonderful individual display from Pjani, as he dribbled past <a href="/wiki/Sulley_Muntari" title="Sulley Muntari">Sulley Muntari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Montolivo" title="Riccardo Montolivo">Riccardo Montolivo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Adil_Rami" title="Adil Rami">Adil Rami</a> before putting the ball in the net.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 May 2014, Pjani signed a new contract which will last until 30 June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In a friendly tournament in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> in July, he scored from inside his own half, but Roma lost 3–2 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Serie_A" title="2014–15 Serie A">2014–15 season</a>, he became considered as a rising star in Italian football, scoring 5 times and assisting 10 goals.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_A.S._Roma_season" title="2015–16 A.S. Roma season">2015–16 season</a>, Pjani emerged as one of the world's finest free-kick takers, netting a brilliant goal against <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> on 30 August and scoring several more, including in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>. By the January break, he had scored 7 goals and assisted another 5, being linked with a transfer to <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and Real Madrid in the winter transfer window.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Towards the end of the season, rumours spread in the media of Pjani's possible departure from Roma, as he was linked with Juventus.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season with ten league goals, and 12 in all competitions, while also finishing the league season as the top assist provider in Serie A for the second consecutive season, alongside Juventus' <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pogba" title="Paul Pogba">Paul Pogba</a>, with 12 assists.<sup id="cite_ref-assists_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assists-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Juventus">Juventus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Juventus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus,_10_August_2019_(7)_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus%2C_10_August_2019_%287%29_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid_v_Juventus,_10_August_2019_(7)_-_Miralem_Pjani%C4%87_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pjani attempts a free kick for <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the 2019–20 preseason</div></div></div>
<p>On 13 June 2016, Pjani joined <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> on a five-year contract for a fee of €32 million, ending a five-year stint with Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He chose the number 5 shirt to start the new season.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On 10 September, Pjani scored on his debut in a 3–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/U.S._Sassuolo_Calcio" title="U.S. Sassuolo Calcio">Sassuolo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> After winning <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Coppa_Italia" title="2016–17 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Serie_A" title="2016–17 Serie A">Serie A</a> in his first season, he missed out on a potential <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>, having lost in the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2017 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League Final</a> to Real Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani's second season at Juventus began with a 2–3 loss against <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2017 Supercoppa Italiana">2017 Supercoppa Italiana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal of the season in <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Mole" title="Derby della Mole">city derby</a> against Torino on 23 September 2017. Juventus won the game 4–0.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On 28 February, Pjani scored a crucial penalty against <a href="/wiki/Atalanta_B.C." title="Atalanta B.C.">Atalanta</a> to send Juventus through to the <a href="/wiki/2018_Coppa_Italia_Final" title="2018 Coppa Italia Final">2018 Coppa Italia Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Juventus won that final, with Pjani contributing by assisting for one of the goals in a convincing triumph over Milan on 9 May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Pjani once again became Serie A champion in a game against his old club Roma, which sealed his second domestic <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> in two seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On 19 May, the final match of the season, he scored his fifth league goal of the season, netting a trademark free kick, which sealed Juventus's 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Hellas_Verona_F.C." title="Hellas Verona F.C.">Hellas Verona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the beginning of his <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Juventus_F.C._season" title="2018–19 Juventus F.C. season">third campaign</a> with the club, Pjani put pen to paper on a new five-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal of the season in a 2–0 home win over Lazio on 25 August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 19 September, in his first <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> game of the season, Pjani helped his team to a win by converting two penalties against <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a> in an eventual 2–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On 6 October, in a game against <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a>, he made his 100th appearance for Juventus.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 September 2019, Pjani won his 100th match with Juventus in all competitions in a 2–1 home win over Verona in Serie A.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 July 2020, he won his fourth league title with the club after defeating <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> 2–0 at home.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He made his final appearance for the club on 7 August, in a 2–1 home win over his former club Lyon in the second leg of the round of 16 of the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2019–20 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>; however, despite the victory, the result saw Juventus eliminated from the competition on away goals following a 2–2 aggregate draw.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Barcelona">Barcelona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Barcelona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 29 June 2020, Juventus announced that they had reached an agreement with <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> for the transfer of Pjani on a deal worth €60&#160;million, plus a maximum of €5&#160;million in bonuses, to be effective following the conclusion of the 2019–20 season. The deal was also coordinated with a swap of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Melo" title="Arthur Melo">Arthur Melo</a>, whom Juve signed for €72&#160;million, plus a maximum of €10&#160;million in bonuses.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Pjani signed a contract with the Spanish side for the next four seasons, until the end of the 2023–24 campaign, with a buy-out clause of €400 million.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut on 27 September, coming on as a substitute in a 4–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/Villarreal_CF" title="Villarreal CF">Villareal</a> in La Liga.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to spending his childhood in Luxembourg, Pjani became eligible for <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">their national team</a> and begun representing the nation's youth sides. He represented Luxembourg in the <a href="/wiki/2006_UEFA_European_Under-17_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship">2006 European Under-17 Championship</a>, for which Luxembourg qualified automatically as hosts. He scored Luxembourg's only goal of the tournament. In that same year, he scored 4 goals in a match against Belgium, which ended in a 5–5 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Before making his decision regarding his national team status, Pjani was eligible to represent Luxembourg and Bosnia and Herzegovina.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_(edited).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg/170px-20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg/255px-20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg/340px-20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_%28edited%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="659" data-file-height="990" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2108_AUT_BIH_2382_(edited).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pjani playing for <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2008, during an interview for Bosnian newspaper, Pjani stated that he wanted to play for <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, officials in the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Football Association of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Football Association of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> took notice and Pjani was called-up to the <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_under-21_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national under-21 football team">country's under-21 team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> However, because Pjani no longer had a Bosnian passport and needed <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> approval to switch nationalities, he wasn't allowed to be called-up for the senior team. After an eight-month wait and following the involvement of <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Kom%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Željko Komši">Željko Komši</a>, a member of the three-person <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, Pjani received a Bosnian passport in early 2008.
</p><p>He debuted for Bosnia and Herzegovina on 20 August 2008 in the team's 1–2 loss to <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On 3 March 2010, he scored his first senior international goal in Bosnia's 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pjani was instrumental in Bosnia and Herzegovina's qualification for <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, their first major competition, and he was named in 23-men squad for the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He debuted in the team's opening group match, a narrow defeat to <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Maracan%C3%A3" class="mw-redirect" title="Estádio do Maracanã">Estádio do Maracanã</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On 25 June, during the final group match against <a href="/wiki/Iran_national_football_team" title="Iran national football team">Iran</a>, Pjani scored a goal, leading to a 3–1 victory to help Bosnia and Herzegovina to their first ever FIFA World Cup win.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nicknamed <i>"il Piccolo Principe"</i> <i>("the Little Prince")</i> during his time with Roma,<sup id="cite_ref-repubblica.it-pjanic-Prince_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-repubblica.it-pjanic-Prince-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Pjani was regarded as one of the most promising young midfielders of his generation in his youth,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and was included in <a href="/wiki/Don_Bal%C3%B3n" title="Don Balón">Don Balón</a>'s list of the 100 best young players in the world in 2010;<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> however, he was also thought to lack composure at times in the media.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> His Juventus manager Massimiliano Allegri touted him as a potentially world class midfielder in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> later also adding that, although he was extremely talented, he needed to stay more "calm and focused" in order to fulfil his potential;<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> subsequently, the 2016–17 season saw him establish himself as one of the best, most skillful, and most versatile midfielders in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Although he is neither particularly quick, nor gifted with athleticism or physical strength,<sup id="cite_ref-profile_–_Miralem_Pjanic_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile_–_Miralem_Pjanic-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Pjani has been described as an efficient "old-fashioned <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> with huge technical qualities".<sup id="cite_ref-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>A talented, creative, and tenacious <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a>, with quick feet, Pjani is usually deployed in a <a href="/wiki/Central_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Central midfielder">central midfield</a> role, or as a <a href="/wiki/Deep-lying_playmaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep-lying playmaker">deep-lying playmaker</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Defensive_midfielder" title="Midfielder">front of the back-line</a>, although his tactical versatility, defensive awareness, and work-rate enable him to play in several midfield positions, and he has also been used in more advanced roles as an offensive-minded central midfielder, known as the "<a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Mezzala" title="Midfielder">mezzala</a>" role, in Italian, or even as an <a href="/wiki/Attacking_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Attacking midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PDV_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDV-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-beINSports_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beINSports-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dipende_da_Pjanic_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dipende_da_Pjanic-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sconto_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sconto-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-who_is_the_Roma_midfielder?_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who_is_the_Roma_midfielder?-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (September 2020)">excessive citations</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and has even been deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a> on occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Pjani's main attributes are his range of passing, <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills, and vision, which make him an excellent <a href="/wiki/Assist_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Assist (football)">assist</a> provider, and also enable him to dictate the tempo of his team's play in midfield and orchestrate goalscoring opportunities for his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miralem_Pjanic_a_major_boost_to_Juventus&#39;_hopes_of_European_glory-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PDV_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PDV-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-beINSports_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beINSports-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dipende_da_Pjanic_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dipende_da_Pjanic-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Known for his eye for goal from midfield and striking ability from distance,<sup id="cite_ref-beINSports_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beINSports-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Pjani is also known for having the capacity to get into good scoring positions by making late attacking runs into the penalty area from behind.<sup id="cite_ref-dipende_da_Pjanic_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dipende_da_Pjanic-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sconto_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sconto-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lanci_di_Miralem_Pjanic-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> A renowned <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">set-piece specialist</a>, he is highly regarded for his accurate, <a href="/wiki/Curl_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Curl (football)">bending</a> free-kicks, as well as his delivery from dead-ball situations; in 2015, he was described as the best free-kick taker in the world by renowned set-piece specialist and former Lyon teammate <a href="/wiki/Juninho_Pernambucano" title="Juninho Pernambucano">Juninho</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beINSports_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beINSports-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Pjani's precocious talent, playmaking skills, and ability to score many goals from free kicks saw him labelled as a potential heir to Juninho at Lyon.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> However, despite his ability and the praise he has garnered from pundits, due to his elegant and creative playing style, Pjani has also drawn criticism on occasion in the media for being inconsistent,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> while Livio Caferoglu of <i><a href="/wiki/Football_Italia" title="Football Italia">Football Italia</a></i> accused him of being "too slight to impose himself as a defensive midfielder," and "too slow to release the ball."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Pjani is a <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Bosniak" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak">ethnic Bosniak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> He has a son named Edin with his longtime girlfriend, Josepha from <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Along with his native <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, Pjani is fluent in six additional languages: <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish" title="Luxembourgish">Luxembourgish</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 Pjani was enrolled at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sarajevo" title="University of Sarajevo">University of Sarajevo</a>, majoring in sport and physical education.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, while playing for <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a>, he stated: "I have followed <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a> since the days of <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">[Zinedine] Zidane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, when I fell in love. Since then, it is my preferred club and it always will be."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Later, when he was a <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> player, he confirmed that he had been a fan of Real Madrid since his childhood.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Juventus_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Juventus F.C. season">2017–18 season</a>, Pjani appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Television_documentary" title="Television documentary">docu-series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/First_Team:_Juventus" title="First Team: Juventus">First Team: Juventus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Corsa_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corsa-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 August 2020, Pjani tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a> amid its <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Italy" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Italy">pandemic in Italy</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> by 8 September, he recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miralem_Pjani%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
